<Author>CAM66
<Content>Nice hotel, good value  We stayed for two nights between Christmas and New Year in one of the Comfort level double bed rooms. On arrival the staff were friendly and throughout our stay they were always helpful. The room itself was clean, a decent size, by Parisienne standards, and looked like it had recently been refreshed/decorated. The facilities inside the room were good including a mini-bar service, flat screen T.V. and modern/new shower unit. The only things worthy of critical comment are pretty minimal, however so that others are aware: if you stay in rooms at the end of a corridor you need to know where the light switch is, to illuminate the area in front of your door, otherwise it can be quite difficult to see the handle and unlock the door. Once you've found the light ouside the door for the first time it's no problem from then on. There are some areas with suspended panels for the celing and when you open/close a door the pressure can sometimes cause these to move and they can startle you a little. Finally, like many older buildings you can hear most every noise in the rooms around you. This is just the way things are in older built apartments  hotels and simply cannot be avoided. So, minor criticisms aside, overall we liked this hotel, it has a good location and is near the Metro and Rue Cler market/cafe areas, where there are several excellent little bistro's and retaurants. We would happily stay again.

<Author>yamato8
<Content>An Honest Review Hotel Duquesne Eiffel is a small hotel rated at 3 stars. Comparing to other hotels of similar class, the room size is a bit small but very clean. The furnishings are new, tasteful and comfortable. They have free Internet access which is a plus. However, their elevator is small and made a jerking motion everytime it stops at a floor. After using it several times, we got the hang of it. Location is very good since it is near a Metro station and some notable spots like Rue de Cler, and the Eiffel Tower. Area also felt very safe.Glitch we experienced during our stay was that the hotel staff who checked us in did not give us a complete orientation. Finding our room was a bit difficult since the hallways were dark. The motion sensitive lights in the hallways on our floor did not always work. Also, staff did not tell us on how to turn on the lights in our room. We were supposed to insert the card key in the light switch to turn on the power. Then our safe did not have a key and we were given the option to leave our valuables in the front desk. Not that we did not appreciate the effort by Julie. Thanks to her we were able to go around the city without worrying about the safety of our travel documents, etc. Jessica was equally helpful in giving tips on which sights to see and also provided logistics on how to get to those places. Even the guy who checked us in was helpful in providing us hot drinking water late at night for my grandmother's tea. Probably he just needs more training on how to entertain guests. Lastly, breakfast could use more variety. They served eggs and ham everyday. Maybe they can mix it up with bacon and sunny side up some other days.Overall, we enjoyed our stay in this hotel and would therefore recmommend it.

<Content>Roaches? We booked this hotel because of the high ratings on Trip Advisor. While it did live up to what many people have written about in terms of the recent remodeling, our big problems was probable tiny roaches! <Author>scarpia
<Content>A very nice place to call home in Paris.. Winding up a positive 8-day stay. Here's how this place paid off:-- Quiet rooms! Paris can be noisy, but not here. If you need 2 rooms ask for 17 and 18, end units so no shared walls with others and you can create a mini-suite by locking an outside hallway door.-- Rooms recently redone, clean and well appointed. We found the beds comfy, nice bedding, a good night's rest through the jetlag.-- Helpful, hard-working front desk. Estelle and Julie are formidable one-two punch, proactive on problem solving, fast online with reservations, etc., better English than one would find in Paris, Tx.-- Location, location, loc... you get the point. 3-minute walk to Metro, 5-minute to Napoleon's mausoleum, Invalides, 10-minutes Rodin museum, 15-minutes to Eiffel Tower. Best of all, just off Rue Clare 5 minutes to stunning fromagerie Marie Anne Cantin, another 30 seconds to equally awesome boulangerie Pain d'Epis, both Top 10 Paris ratings. Gives you Paris' best meal under 10 Euros if you bring it back to the room.-- A word about the 7th. Pleasant and very safe, but for slamming nightlife you'll need to Metro elsewhere. Some nice cafes and parks adjacent, but this is not the spot for clubbing.-- And full disclosure asterisk. As I sit here typing, about the only downside that comes to mind is that rooms can run small for a standard, as does the bathroom.

<Author>the-savman
<Content>Nice hotel This is a very well maintained property in good location near the Eiffel Tower and very close to the Metro station for exploring Paris. The rooms are very small but spotless, cosy feel and v comfortable bed.The hotel is very expensive for what it is but that seems to be the norm for the City as a whole. Free internet access in the lobby for hotel guests which is a very nice feature. We did not sample breakfast as we did not feel it was worth 鈧?2pp when there were cheaper alternatives within very close walking distance in the many cafes etc.One seemingly insignificant grips, but irritating nonetheless, is the total lack of any English channels on the in room TV, not even by PPV. If you do not speak French you will go bonkers if you have to spend any long spells relaxing in your room. Very strange considering one would assume this property would attract many international visitors and to not even have a basic news channel to watch is frustrating (let alone Hollywood movies badly overdubbed).Minor issues aside, we would recommend the Duquesne for first time visitors to Paris, it's in a good neighbourhood with decent accessibility to everywhere. If returning we would probably stay elsewhere but that's taking nothing away from this very nice hotel.The staff were generally friendly although (just a tip) when your guests are checking out in the early morning and request a taxi, it's not good etiquette to send them out onto the cold dark streets to hail down a cab to try save some call out charges. Good intention perhaps, but we nearly missed our connecting airport coach transfer (hardly worth the stress for 鈧?).There was also no tea/coffee making facilities in the room which we found strange but there was a chargeable minibar if one was so inclined.  
<Date>Oct 1, 2008

<Author>jchin1
<Content>Awesome Hotel We stayed here for 2 separate stints in our Europe trip.1st part:Arrived early afternoon at Hotel Duquesne and they told us that we didn't have room for 1 night out of 3 nights, and that the booked us a room at the Hotel Splendid down the street. We stupidly agreed to this arrangement not knowing that Splendid wasn't so splendid. the only redeeming part was that we had a view of the Eiffel Tower from our hotel window. But after getting our room at Duquesne the next day (they took our bags for us), we realized that Duquesne was so much nicer. We didnt' have a view of the Tower, but the bed, bathroom and room was so much nicer. Breakfast was covered for us, because of their mishap, which was great. Eggs, ham, good coffee, etc.2nd part:came back to Hotel Duquesne after a couple more cities in Europe and it felt like home instantly. They gave us a room on the 4th floor with a perfect view of the Eiffel. If we go back I'll definitely request that room.Great location, 7 minute run to the Eiffel Tower, right by some good brasseries/cafes, metro, clean rooms, good breakfast, pleasant service, decent price. When i go back to Paris I'll definitely book here again.

<Author>travel_addict_92
<Content>Perfect for Paris! I was very excited about staying in this hotel, for starters, it was one of the only ones in our price range without cheap old furniture, two it was being renovated, three the eiffel tower being sooo close!We arrived around 10pm, checkin was quick and easy, however lift is quite small as expected! So one person at a time when up with their luggage. We were in a room known as La Sorbonne. It was a very nice triple room, with a seperate toilet, and two windows. The beds are incredibly comfortable! Considering you will be walking around all day they are the best to just relax in. I've read many reviews about the breakfast not being good. well my family LOVED the breakfast. For 12 Euro, you got croissants, bread, canned fruit, scramble eggs, bacon, pastries etc. 12 Euro sounds like a lot, but on wkends the bakery next door is not open and it's about 2 blocks till you get to a cafe for breakfast and you're looking to pay 8Euro for tea/coffee, croissant and bread. Where as at the hotel you get a semi cooked breakfast and you can have as much as you like. Maids in the breakfast room dont speak much english but they are very friendly and helpful. As far as food in the area goes, there were VERY few restaurants. Especially family style ones. Sure they had a few restaurants but with interesting menu choices, i know this is france, but you could have some trouble finding food. We found a very nice lebanese restaurant that served mixed grills which were so good and although their menu is not in english the friendly elderly man is more then willing to translate. Unfortunately i can't remember the name of the place but its next to a restaurant called Pizza Tina's. Anothe place we ate at, it was ok. Location wise, its a residential, quiet street, close to the L'open Invalides stop about 3-5min walk. The Eiffel tower is around a 15-20min walk. Front desk staff were very helpful, specially Lucie who organised us euro disney passes, l'open passes, metro advice etc, however always ask to book a taxi in advance, never listen if they say you dont need to book one an hour ahead. As we had a show at 7 and were waiting and waiting for a taxi, as we were told we wouldnt have to wait and there was no need to ring ahead. Insist on ringing ahead!!

<Author>jrk_23
<Content>Best Bed EVER! We stayed at the Duquesne for 5 nights to start off our European honeymoon. The staff were very courteous at the front desk and showed us to the room. Everything in the hotel is small. The lobby is small, the elevator is tiny and the hallways are tight but that's Paris for you. The Room: The room was TINY!!! It was room 10 and it was basically a bed with about 6 inches on either side. The bathroom was tiny as well as only one person could stand at it at a time. There was no real storage in the hotel room either but that being said, it was the most comfortable bed ever and we slept well into the first morning there. The next day we requested an upgrade and were immediately shown a deluxe room that was still small by North American standards but was much more appropriate. The Staff: For the most part we were very pleased with them. They all spoke good english and were able to help us with any problem. They were having a computer problem while we were there so our upgrade took some time but as we ended up with what we wanted, we arent' going to complain.The Location: Great location, close to metro and the Eiffel tower. No complaints there.Food: The breakfast there is not included and at 11 euros, I would suggest grabbing a croissant or baguette at the patisserie on up the road. The thai place next door is indeed really good.All in all, while it was not the nicest hotel we stayed in on our honeymoon, it was a very comfortable stay and we would recommend it, although only the upgraded room. We also stayed at the Plaza Tour Eiffel which has a higher trip advisor rating and I would stay in the Duquesne over it.

<Author>AlbertaRocky
<Content>Excellent Choice My wife, teenaged son  I stayed at the Duquesne Eiffel Hotel for four nights in the beginning of July and couldn't have asked for a better hotel. We had booked a triple room (with a view of the Eiffel Tower if possible) and were given separate adjoining rooms, one with a view out the window if you open it and look to the right. The rooms, not large but adequate, were recently renovated to a very high standard and had very comfortable beds. The weather was fairly warm for a couple of the days we stayed and the air conditioning was a great relief after a full day of walking and touring. The rooms were very quiet as other reviewers had mentioned because of the new windows. The staff was very helpful at the desk and the cleaning staff do an outstanding job.It was our first (and definitely not last) trip to Paris and the location was perfect for going to the Eiffel Tower, Napolean's Tomb (really worthwhile) and excellent restaurants. The Metro is great for getting around anywhere and the station is a five minute walk. Paris is a truly great city and our stay at the Duquesne Eiffel Hotel made it all the better. I do not hesitate to recommend staying here.

<Author>Tigerlight206
<Content>It's a great as everyone says! It's everything we hoped it would be! I don't have much to add to everyone else's positive review except that I wholeheartedly agree. This is a wonderful European hotel. Having travelled all over Europe, this is one of my favorites.With it's charming rooms, comfy beds, good air conditioning, reasonably priced minibars, and helpful/quirky english speaking staff, this is a particularly good choice for Americans. Some of the rooms are quite small, and you'll surely get a chuckle from the elevator, but that's Europe. And if your lucky enough to get a view..... oh my do they have them!!!! The staff can be a teensy bit touchy if you try to request a view, but just understand they don't really charge extra for the views specifically which means everyone wants it and not everyone can have it... just ask nicely and be patient. We didn't think the breakfast was all that spectacular but there are many alternative choices in the area and it's optional. Some fresh fruit (not out of a can) would have been nice as part of the breakfast...All in all, an excellent choice.

<Author>L878765
<Content>Safe, clean, affordable, well located, welcoming and stylish Wow - where to start? It is an excellent hotel, and the best value hotel I have used in Paris. I've been visiting Paris for 20 years and this is the best hotel (but not the most expensie) I've stayed in. Excellent location in a pleasant, quiet but very central area. Close to metro, but you can walk to many places in central Paris from the hotel. You can also stock up on mineral water, fruit, bread etc in shops nearby. The hotel is very stylish, in fact I'd say it is sophisticated - I got the impression that someone with an interior design background has been involved in this or they've paid a lot to get a good professional designer in. The room I stayed in was very nicely decorated and furnished - in fact better than most 4 star hotels I have stayed in. Everything was perfect, including the choice of paint colour on the woodwork and the inspired striped carpet! The lighting was unusually good - with all the lights on it was bright enough for me to read by, I'm really sick of dismal rooms when you turn the lights on full and you still can't read. Reception staff spoke fluent English, were efficient, friendly, and more approachable and helpful than I have found before in a Paris hotel. The breakfast serving staff were great also - good English, friendly, helpful. I'm not one for asking a lot of questions of reception staff, but I noticed some other English speaking guests doing so and the receptionist was really helping with advice, hints etc. Both check-in and check-out were rapid.The reason I booked here and not another place? Fire safety. I have a thing about it, and, being English, despair of why such an advanced country as France doesn't have the same standards we insist on in hotels in the UK. I only book Paris hotels if there are smoke detectors, which rules a lot of them out! And there are mains-wired detectors, and alarms, in the public areas - so I felt safe. But there didn't seem to be a smoke detector or alarm in my room. I was disappointed about this - I had read on some website (maybe not the hotel one, but one of the many that carry details about hotels) that there were smoke detectors or alarms in each room. If there was a detector or alarm in my room I could not find it. However, I would stay again - it's well built, and as well as the public areas coverage there was a sturdy fire door to segregate the bit of corridor my room was in from the rest of the corridor, and so I felt entirely safe. (PS I wish reviewers on tripadvisor would comment on this feature - a couple of years ago I stayed in a very positively reviewed Paris Hotel that I thought was a death-trap, with no smoke detectors or alarms - and yet there were dozens of people who'd written how nice the receptionists were! Hotels like this one, that invest in safety, should be acknowledged for this). Good quality flat screen tv with reasonable range of channels. A great view of the Eiffel Tower, shimmering and glittering. On a reasonably busy road but not too bad, and the double (or is it triple?) glazing highly effective. Good plumbing, in fact very good - easy to get the temperature balance right, and a proper shower screen (which you don't always get in Paris). I stay in hotels quite a lot, and this one was unusually clean. There is not even a hint of limescale build-up anywhere in the bathroom, and no dust. You get the impression that someone obsessive about quality is involved in running this hotel. Attention to detail is everywhere. I didn't use it, but there was a laptop with internet access and checking it briefly it seemed to be working okay. Oh, and whilst it's a newspaper I abhor and never buy because it attacks my home city (Liverpool), the English newspaper The Guardian was stocked. Nice for those English liberals, public servants and Liverpool-haters out there. Bed comfortable - I prefer a firm mattress and found it ok, not as hard as I like at home, but a good hard hotel firm. If I stay somewehre with a soft mattress I usualy end up sleeping on the floor, but no such problem here. I slept very well. Noise between rooms was a bit of a mystery to me so hard to judge after just one stay of just one night. Generally I think it's very good indeed - for an old building excellent. However, the doors close noisily and someone staying in a room close to me came back late and seemed to open and close the door a lot......the hall lights (movement activated?) may have confused them, I don't know. It woke me up. But no noise of neighbouring bathrooms (which is common in old converstions) or of TVs, which makes me think the sound insulation is good. I think if you are noise-phobic (as I am, as well as being fire-phobic and rudeness-phobic) you will probably get on well with this hotel. What can be improved? The quality of breakfast was acceptable but a bit disappointing for the price (12 euro) despite the lovely staff. Coffee in particular was a let-down - murky and just quite not good enough. I mainly stay in English hotels, where the quality of coffee has come on hugely in recent years, and sadly Paris hotels (this one is not alone) aren't quite there with coffee at the moment. Choice of food very limited. Just not quite good enough for the money. Okay, don't be put off, it's not a deal-breaker, but I think it could be improved. Served in a lovely stone room. The minibar prices are not at all good! 2.50 for a packet of crisps!!!!!!!!!! (chips to Americans). I know all hotels charge a lot for minibars, but with the pound-exchange rate being so bad, it just hurt as I arrived hungry and raided the mini-bar! Lots of little shops nearby, so don't make my mistake! So there are two things that I think might be improved, but obviously everything comes at a price, and the price for the room was excellent, so I won't complain too loudly. At last I have found a hotel in Paris I really like, and feel comfortable and safe in that doesn't cost a fortune! Whoever is repsonsible for all this, well done and thank you.

<Author>kate026
<Content>My Home Away From Home I just completed an 11 night stay at this hotel (business and vacation mixed.) Having been to Paris three times previously, I have decided that nowhere could be better than the Hotel Duquesne Eiffel in the 7th Arr. (neighborhood area). I read a lot of reviews on Trip Advisor and decided this time on the Hotel Duquesne Eiffel--and I didn't go wrong! It is a charming hotel located across from the Ecole Militaire and about a block from Les Invalides in a beautiful area of boulevards, trees, and lovely cafes. Cross the boulevard, and walk directly to the Champs du Mars, the gorgeous park in which sits the Eiffel Tower! Just two blocks from the hotel is the Rue Cler market street (think chocolate, wine, flowers). Julie, the hotel's manager is a dream to work with. She helped me make the reservation directly with the hotel (and didn't get frustrated at all when my travel dates had to change). All of the staff are fluent in English and were most helpful in making reservations, taxi services, and offering directions. As an addicted-to-ice American, I even had that available from the lower-level kitchen! My room was lovely, and large compared to other places I have stayed in Paris. Of course, I was most fortunate to have a room on the 5th floor with a gorgeous view of the Eiffel Tower, glittering at night like a diamond pendant hanging from the sky. The hotel has recently undergone a decor change (from most online photos). The subtle tones of ecru, plum, green, and burgundy are most relaxing after a long day of working, walking, and sight seeing. The rooms are cleaned daily and everything in my room and bath was always spotless! Breakfast at the hotel is a bargain, particularly with a large pot of coffee, juice, eggs, and all of the wonderful pastries of Paris. Convenient to the hotel is the metro stop---the easiest and fastest way to get around Paris. From my metro I could travel with no difficulty to the area of the Louvre, Grand Boulevards, the Marais, Latin Quarter, and the outer areas of Paris. If you are going to Paris, make sure not to overlook the Hotel Duquesne. Although listed as a 3 star hotel, I give this darling spot a 5 star rating in every way!

<Author>johnriggins
<Content>Excellent Location, Helpful, Friendly Staff Stayed at the Hotel Duquesne Eiffel for 3 nights in May 2008.Very efficient check-in by helpful, English speaking staff. Found all staff over the duration of our stay to be very friendly and only too willing to assist. Hotel is about 200 metres from Ecole Militaire Metro station with good connections to CDG Airport.As you would expect, the bedrooms are not huge but they are well-appointed and very clean. Free internet access in the lounge and a small bar.Very convenient location, as the name implies it is only 10 minutes walk from the Eiffel Tower and 5 from Les Invalides with Napoleon's Tomb. If, like us, you are looking for a comfortable base in a nice area for a few days, I would certainly recommend this hotel. Plenty restaurants within a 5 minute walk and lots of bars. Little or no traffic noise during the night even though we had a room which overlooked the main street.Found Paris to be more expensive than previous visits due to the Euro exchange rate. Still a wonderful place to visit with a multitude of things to see and do. Beware of con artists pretending to have just found a large gold ring beside you and willing to give it to you for a few euros - watched a few of them try this well-rehearsed routine with unsuspecting tourists.

<Author>Willneverreturnagain
<Content>TOTALLY UNORGANIZED At first we were impressed by the location (quiet avenue, walking distance from the Eiffel Tower) and the fact that the rooms had been recently renovated and everything was super clean.But later the true quality of this hotel was revealed. First, the air conditioning was not working properly, so the 2 rooms we had were a hot as a sauna. The very friendly but absolutely incompetent girl at the desk simply apologized but did not provide any kind of solution. We were basically told to grin and bear it, as it was a holiday in Paris and there was no staff to fix it. Changing rooms was not a possibility either. Later on the day, we asked for an iron, which of course was not available in the room. My husband was sent to a steamy room in the basement and had to iron his shirt himself, as again, there was no staff/laundry service available. The last straw was when, having tickets for the Opera, we asked Reception to book a taxi for us with an hour in advance. The girl said that it was not necessary to book it that early, as 10 minutes was enough. Of course, the taxi she called was over 15 minutes late, so we started to get worried and went out to the street to get one ourselves. Guess what? When we are sitting inside the car, already running late and risking missing the show we had booked months in advance, she ran outside to the street, opened the door, and demanded us to get off the car immediately as she had already called a taxi for us and we could not cancel it. We replied it was her own fault as she had evidently called it too late, but she was mad and demanded the taxi driver to stop. Just then the other taxi arrived, and we were forced to get in it. By the time we got there, we barely had time to get to our seats a minute before it started. We were so stressed and shocked that the whole evening was ruined. Oh, and did I mention that the transfer she booked for us to pick us from the airport was ALSO 20 minutes late? To sum up, the administration of the hotel is completely unreliable, so if you decide to stay there, be prepared to book all your services independently and deal with the insane girl at the front desk. After the taxi incident she was SO rude that we were actually happy to leave Paris.

<Content>What a waste of time! I was really impressed with the reviews and recommendations for this hotel so quickly put it in my top 3 to look into. I was after a balcony and view so decided to contact the hotel directly to make an enquiry. I explained very clearly that we require a room with balcony and view and were wanting this confirmed before we made the booking, as we were going to enquire with many hotels until we got what we were after. I advised I would not book if I could not have this. We were happy to ask around as not going to Paris until August 08.So, after their reply with what they could offer for our dates, we kept up the communication and booked a room- only to be informed once we booked and paid a booking fee, that the rooms we were after were all gone!!!! Oh but you can have another nice one that is not what you want....typical dodgy hotel tricks. I know hotels do it, cos most people will take what they are given but I had one requirement so not good enough for me!I was really disappointed with this hotels service and I sent a couple of emails asking why I was not told in the first place that they did not have any rooms available with my requirements, but they avoided the question, just advising they are limited and what we can have etc.So I have sent a final reply to them  requested it be passed to the manager but unsurprisingly, now that I have cancelled the booking I have not heard a peep from them...All other replies came back within 1/2 a day and now its been 3 or so days without a word. Since I am not going to be giving them any more money I guess they just dont care what I think, I am just one chump in many. Be very careful when you have specific requirements...make sure you get a straight answer from them or you might get the broom closet.The fact that they do not have a room for us is fine, I understand they have a limited number. Thats why I asked first! What really annoys me is that they should have been honest in their reply to my enquiry. I was very clear that we needed this confirmed before booking and they pretty much just tricked us into booking. Not what I call good service at all. I will never look at staying here again simply due to the appalling service. And its not just one staff member, my initial query was answered my the Manager Julie herself. I am sure its a nice hotel and I would have liked to see that, instead I was mucked around by an incompetent, dishonest hotel business.What makes me laugh (now) is that after wasting 4 days in correspondence with this I hotel, I enquired with Hotel Les Jardins d'Eiffel...not expecting much after this experience as I was very annoyed with the whole thing, packing a sad n all that. But they were friendly, helpful and honest in what they could offer. So I now have my perfect hotel room for my anniversary, with a balcony and view of the Eiffel tower- just at a different hotel! I will of course let everyone know if it worked out....

<Author>Dempsies
<Content>Immaculate and great location! My fiance and I stayed in the hotel for 3 nights from the 18th April in an inside double room. We had high expectations based on the other reviews, and I'm glad to say we were in no way disappointed. Professional, attentive and friendly staff in reception who are a credit to the hotel. Room was immaculate, modern and although was on the small side it had everything we needed and more (mini-bar, flat screen tv and a very comfy bed). Great location with only a 10 minute walk to the Eiffel Tower and a couple of minutes to the Ecole Militaire metro station. Thai restaurant next door was very good and some good pavement bars beside the metro station where we enjoyed several late night bottles of wine. Would recommend this hotel to my friends and would definitely go back. (Would book a superior upgraded room to try and get a view of the Eiffel Tower twinkling at night, although this cannot be guaranteed). Rooms on the top floor have a balcony! Suggestion = some background music in the reception area/bar would be nice to listen to when having a drink. Everything else was PERFECT.P.S (Experienced some rather rude and arrogant staff in other french restaurants - one waiter argued that I wouldn't need a side order of fries with my dinner . I am a big eating tiny woman!! Another refused to let us sit at an unreserved outside table where we could both see the Eiffel Tower because it was a table for 4 people. This was at 11pm and the place was half empty!!)

<Author>C0unt
<Content>Great Hotel!! My wife and I stayed at the Hotel Duquesne during our stay in Paris. We originally booked our stay there because of the reviews we read on tripadvisor.com and because it was so close to the sites in the Invalides area. The hotel was very clean and all of the front desk were extremely polite and helpful. The floor our room was on had some renovations but there was nothing in the way and the room we stayed in was beautifully renovated. We had a magnificent view of the Eiffel Tower and even though hotel rooms in Paris are quite small the room we had was quite large. The room had a very comfortable Queen size bed, small desk, spacious closet, mini bar, in room safe and detached bathroom with a full tub/shower. The hotel is quite close to some great restaurants, cafes, many scenic sites including the Eiffel Tower and close to the Metro also. There is breakfast served in the morning for an additional fee but we always ate at a cafe near by. The rates were very reasonable and this is one Hotel I would stay at again!! I definitely recommend it to anyone looking for a great place to stay in Paris.

<Author>ortonioni
<Content>A room with a view Getting a nice hotel in a big European city at a price you can afford can be a problem. The Duquesne (pronounce it Ducain or the taxi drivers wont understand you) was recommended by friends so we knew it would be fine. We were not disappointed and like most of the reviewers here we would highly commend the staff. Yes the rooms are small - that's the compromise. For a similar price in other European cities you would be lucky to get the cleanliness and comfort of the rooms and the peaceful, spacious location. The avenues around the hotel are wide and the streets are populated but not crowded, so you feel safe walking home at night.We didn't bother with breakfast in the hotel as there are nice bakeries, cafes and brasseries nearby and it was fun to check them out each morning - these are all cheaper than the hotel too.We ate some fantastic evening meals in Paris but I'll just mention the best one locally here - Le P'tit Troquet, 28 rue de l'Exposition. It only has about 6 or 7 tables and is like sitting in an antiques shop. At 32 Euros for 3 courses we thought it was great value for such quality. English is spoken and we felt it was a nice discreet French experience. There are livelier places - the hotel recommends No 7 de vins for some reason, but we found their food bland, mostly cold, and more expensive - though the staff were welcoming and friendly.The mini bar back at the Duquesne is good value as these things go. And a nice half bottle of wine rounds the evening off well. Enjoy Paris!

<Author>LizHeaver
<Content>A fabulous hotel: the perfect base for the perfect holiday. I have just returned from a fabulous stay at this lovely hotel. I took my Mum to Paris to celebrate her 80th birthday, and found this gem of a hotel after hours of internet searching. It really did live up to all the best reviews. Although the hotel is being refurbished at the moment, which meant that the corridors were in the process of being decorated, we were fortunate to be in a newly refurbished room, and everything was immaculate. Very tasteful decor,everything spotlessly clean, and comfortable beds and pillows. The room was big enough and had great wardrobe space and an immaculate bathroom with a great shower and boiling hot water. It took us a long time to work out how to open the mini bar but it was fun trying! We were incredibly lucky to get room 55 with twin beds as I had requested - I draw the line at sharing a double with my mum! The views from 55 are really breathtaking - the tower is so much more impressive by night, and Les Invalides is equally stunning. We could even see Sacre Coeurs in the distance! Obviously not all the rooms can offer this view but it's only a 15 minute walk to get to the real thing and it's a lovely walk too. The location of the hotel is fantastic - metro stations close by and easy to walk to Musee Rodin, Les Invalides and of course to the Tower and River. We also walked to the D'Orsay and across to the Place de La Concorde.The staff at this hotel were brilliant. All spoke perfect English and were so helpful, planning metro routes and offering advice. We would recommend the dinner cruise on the Bateau Parisiennes - at 95 euros it wasn't cheap, but we were treated like royaly, the food was delicious and there was more wine than we could drink, along with great music and the breathtaking views of all the sights along the river. It was a spectacular end to our four day break, and my Mum loved every minute. We recommend the Thai restaurant adjacent to the hotel, and the Italian just round the corner.I can't imagine how anyone could be disappointed by this hotel, and although the view is a bonus, it's still worth visiting because of the lovely decor, comfort, friendly staff and fantastic location. Next time I'll be taking my husband and hopefully leaving the kids at home...

<Author>pcsqueen
<Content>Back Again In May, 2006 we stayed at the hotel while my husband attended a conference at L'Ecole Militaire. When we needed to place to stay during a spur-of-the-moment weekend trip to Paris, I defaulted to this hotel without really considering any other.Coincidentally, we got the same room, #21.While the rooms are indeed small, one must understand that one's in Paris, not Pittsburgh. It's one of the most visited (read: expensive) cities in the world. For the money we spent, I think we received great value. Here's why (and my more general comments apply to both visits):ALL of the staff were friendly, helpful, and thoughtful. The front desk staff, notably Eric, couldn't be nicer or more accommodating. When we arrived early, via the Thalys, he not only got us into an available room, but provided us with coffee, juice, and croissants to raise our energy level. In the evening, he'd greet us and offer a glass of wine or an espresso. Our room, while small, was quite comfortable. We heard no street noise thru the window, and either no guest was inconsiderate or the rooms' soundproofing is excellent .Yes, as one reviewer mentioned, the room's decor was in need of an update; the hotel owner, however, is in the process of completely renovating the entire hotel. Evidently, the upper floors' rooms have been completed and the lower floors and lobby are next in line.The room and bathroom were very clean, as was the rest of the hotel.Beds were comfortable, even to a man with a bad back and arthritic hip, both of which were aggravated by walking the length and breadth of the city.I cannot comment on the breakfast (other than the snack we were offered). With so many wonderful bakeries, cafes, and markets nearby, why eat in the hotel?Additionally, the neighborhood in which the hotel is located is excellent. It's quiet, safe, and relatively non-touristy. The hotel is a short walk to the Metro, and to some of the most lovely streets, IMHO, in Paris. We've decided that it's become our Paris hotel. Now, I've just gotta get another weekend scheduled!

<Author>Aust_mum
<Content>Lovely holiday We stayed for 4 nights and then travelled to the Loire Valley for 3 nights and returned here for 6 more nights with 5 rooms booked for 11 of us. The staff were extremely helpful and kind. The location is good - walking distance to the Eiffel Tower, Napoleon's Tomb. Anywhere in Paris central should be fine as the metro is excellent with stations everywhere if you don't want to walk (unlike Rome!). This area is fairly quiet but has all the necessary markets, patisseries, etc you need within 2 min walk. The sight of the Eiffel Tower out the window every day was magic. You need to have a room number ending in 5 or 6 (preferably 5 as this is the corner) to see it. Do not have a first floor room as the building is lit up at night and the lights shine into the room, no matter how much you fiddle with the curtains! Other floors didn't seem to have this problem. Rooms ending in 4 or 5 have the toilet separate to the bathroom which was very useful. Breakfast is downstairs in the basement so no natural light or view. We ate at local cafes every morning once we got used to just having a croissant or tartine with coffee. Paul's Patisserie chain is excellent - good value, cheap, nice atmosphere. We found it easier to have a good size lunch in a restaurant and then just bread, ham, cheese and wine in our room most nights. Rooms were very clean. We would definitely book this hotel again.

<Author>Morrcoop
<Content>Disappointed This was a hotel choice for a conference I attended in July, so I stayed primarily for the convenience to the conference site. We stayed for over a week and I likely would not stay here again. I feel a bit sheepish writing this review, especially after seeing so many positive ones, but I still think it's important to report about my experiences. Although the front desk staff were certainly pleasant, it鈥檚 affordable, convenient, and the typical size for a European hotel of this quality (as others have stated), it鈥檚 the 鈥渓ittle鈥?things that I noticed that influenced my impression the most (perhaps I noticed them more since I was there for quite a while). Here are just some of my observations 鈥?closet shelving askew (couldn鈥檛 put anything on one of the shelves), shower flooded the floor and toilet with each use, bathroom window could not open fully due to a pipe in the way, dried wax adhered to the carpeting next to the bed (stepped on it every day), wallpaper peeling off the wall in some corners, the light in the hallway outside of our room was dangling by a wire  the lobby doorway leading to the stairs was propped open with a balled-up washcloth. We were in a room on the floor just above the restaurant, and suffered the noise of their cleaning for closing every evening. One day we took a seat on the outdoor chairs and I thought I would write some postcards 鈥?I pulled out a bottle of water I purchased earlier and as I took my first sip, a hotel employee came outside and told me that I needed to enjoy my beverage inside or to please put the beverage away. Of course, if I purchased the beverage from the hotel, I could certainly enjoy it outside. He explained that the hotel was trying to prevent non-hotel guests from walking up and using the tables/chairs as eating areas. I absolutely appreciate the hotel wanting to preserve their property for their guests, but I can hardly believe that sipping from a water bottle would encourage the general populus to enjoy a hearty meal on the hotel doorstep! No wonder I never once saw other hotel guests enjoying the outdoor seating the entire length of my stay. Although we noticed a small bar area in the lobby, he didn鈥檛 offer to sell us a drink 鈥?had he, we would have enjoyed a nice mid-day cocktail. In fact, we were not given any information about the bar during our stay (I did not see a menu in the lobby nor any literature at the front desk or in our room) and it never appeared open for business.For me, a good hotel experience is discovering more than what you expect, not less. If you鈥檙e looking for a Paris hotel for a longish summer stay where attention is paid to the 鈥渓ittle鈥?things, I would not recommend this hotel 鈥?there are so many more options.Lastly, I find it a bit odd that the hotel management responds to almost all of these reviews. TripAdvisor is intended to be a forum for the traveler, and it is surprising that this hotel鈥檚 management monitors every comment 鈥?atypical for this site. Having carefully reviewed our hotel options before booking this hotel, I expected that management would pay as much if not more attention to the little details at the hotel as it does to monitoring this site.

<Author>Pollyanna_7
<Content>Great location Myself and a friend stayed at the Duquesne Eiffel Hotel for 3 nights in November. We had a wonderful trip. We arrived at 10pm in the middle of a massive downpour. The receptionist was joking with us and it lightened our moods. He made a reservation for us at a lovely little Italian restaurant a 5 minute walk away, and we were very happy with this, as we would never have found it on our own. The hotel was kept very clean at all times and the decor is lovely, but I believe they are currently redecorating. We stayed in a twin room called Madeleine; the rooms all seem to be named after areas of Paris. It was a small but perfectly adequate room, the beds were very narrow but I enjoyed a perfect sleep every night. The bathroom was perfect, there was a separate toilet, which was good when there are 2 staying in the room, however a wash hand basin in the toilet room would have been useful. We had a view of the Eiffel Tower from the room, which was fabulous, especially when it sparkles for 10 minutes every hour on the hour. We didn't eat breakfast in the hotel, but enjoyed it along our way out every morning and there were many lovely places to choose from. The drinks in the mini bar were cheap compared to most hotels I have stayed in and compared to the prices in cafes and restaurants around the city. The metro station at Ecole Militaire is very close by, but we found the hotel was very well located for exploring on foot. The Eiffel Tower is very near by and from there, many other sights are within easy walking distance. We even walked back from the Latin quarter late one night and we felt very safe. I would recommend this hotel and I would definitely stay there again.

<Author>RueCler
<Content>Great place to stay We loved our stay at this hotel. It was chosen entirely off the reviews posted here which were spot on. (No, it's not the Ritz but it has everything we needed and more at a price that wasn't too bad.) Our visit was during the transportation strike, but we just walked a lot. There is also a water taxi near the Eiffel Tower that helped out. If there wasn't a strike, this hotel is located near the Metro and multiple bus stops. Many attractions are an easy walk. Also close was Rue Cler, a cobbled pedestrian street with shops/markets selling pastry, flowers, fruits, veggies, merchandise. This was one of our favorite places in Paris (a true cultural experience) and so close to our hotel. Also close were several places to eat; and yes, many menus had English sub-titles. (We learned a few things from the French: take your time eating, enjoy the company, watch the world around you, and relax.) We also found if you know even a few phrases in French, it is very helpful. Buy a Rick Steves' book for help on this. The bathroom of this hotel was very nice given all I've read about hotels in Europe. We had a great view of the Eiffel Tower from our balcony! You've got to see this at night! You'll remember it forever. It was November when we went, so I might suggest a room with a view and no balcony would be fine given the weather. While touring, check out the booksellers along the river starting near the Latin Quarter (also there are great music cafes in this area). Paris was everything we expected it to be and more. This hotel helped make our trip. We'll go back to both as soon as we can!  
<Date>Dec 1, 2007

<Author>bananapancakes1602
<Content>Friendly hotel in a fantastic location We booked the Hotel Duquesne Eiffel for a wedding anniversary long weekend. Having realised the transport strike was in full swing we thought this might put a downer on our trip but it wasn't a problem at all. We got the bus from CDG airport to the Arc de Triumph (13 euros each) and with a half decent map we walked the rest of the way which took about 25mins and was very easy.On arrival at the hotel we were given our key to room 46, a superior room, and some local information, mini bar pricelist etc. The room was pleasantly decorated in lemon and blue with french windows that opened inward to reveal a fantastic view of the Eiffel Tower. The bathroom was spotles with a 3/4 bath and great shower. Good hairdryer too which is quite unusual for hotels. There was also a french window in the bathroom too. The double bed was very comfortable and the heating was very good too, which was a god send because on the sat and sun the weather was very very cold. There were some markings on the wallpaper particularly where the cases would go but overall the room was very clean and tidy and not too small either.Beer in Paris is very expensive. Bottles are 25cl and in the bars cost around 拢3.50gbp and around double for 50cl. Heineken seems to be the popular brand. The prices in the hotel mini bar were probably as cheap as u would find, 25cl bottle of Heineken being around 拢2 a bottle. We didnt eat breakfast in the hotel, We did try the breakfast at the Ecole Militere brasserie down the street which consisted of orange juice, large coffee, french bread and either fried egg with cold ham or scrambled eggs. The cost was around 8 euros. There are lots of cafes and restaurants around the area. We ate at the champ de mars which was very good. There is a great hot food stall, next to the carousel by the Eiffel tower. The hot dogs and fries are delicious.Paris is very easy to get around. All the streets are well signposted and you can literally walk anywhere, weather permitting. The ecole militere metro is a couple of minutes walk down the road if you want to take the tube.All in all we had a lovely time. Paris is a lovely city with lots to offer, and the staff at the hotel Duquesne Eiffel are very helpful and friendly, and for a 3* property, pre refurbishment, i rate it highly. I will definately be returning to both Paris and the Duquesne Eiffel as soon as i can  
<Date>Nov 26, 2007

<Content>Great location, value and staff We had a group of 11 staying at the Duquesne for three nights. <Author>srbmpna
<Content>Nice Hotel, Great Service We stayed at the Duqesne Eiffel for 4 nights-August 30-Sept 3. The hotel is very cute, with a nice outdoor seating area where you can enjoy a drink at the end of a hard day of sighseeing. I am very surprised to hear that other guests found the staff rude--if anything, we found that they went out of their way to make our stay comfortable. One night, I asked the night manager for a couple plastic cups so my husband and I could enjoy a bottle of champagne. He shook his head and disappeared--only to return with champagne flutes and an ice bucket. That's service!The rooms are small, but you're staying in Paris--a major city crammed with centuries-old buildings--there's not a lot of space. The Duquesne is within walking distance of the Tour Eiffel, which is why we chose to stay there. We took many nighttime walks to watch the tower glow and flicker. We'd stay there again.

<Author>jklee92
<Content>Can't say enough good things about Duquesne Eiffel I cannot say enough good things about this hotel and the staff. We just got back from our trip. We found this hotel on tripadvisor.com, and the experience was great. Amandine, Julie and Estelle (and their other team mates) were very helpful (and are still being helpful even though we have already checked out.. more on that later)As this was a wedding anniversary trip, we were very happy to stay at the Duquesne Eiffel.. we stayed in 2 different rooms, #54 and #35 and the view was super.. My birthday was on 8/31, and we were given #35, with the fabulous view of the sparkling eiffel tower, for our last night in Paris. What a super birthday present and way to end our trip to Europe! How many people can really say they had a view of the Eiffel tower? From my first email to our departure, the team at Duquesne Eiffel were very helpful, and thankfully communicated in English very easily (all I had was some junior high school french to rely on!) We stayed a total of 4 nights, and checked out to travel to Belgium for a few days in the middle of the week, and we were able to leave some of our luggage at the hotel, which helped us immensely to be able to travel easier on the trains to Brussels and Brugge, and back to Paris.The location of the hotel is by far the best, in terms of convenience to the metro stop (L'Ecole Militaire), Rue Cler, the Supermarche, as well as the Eiffel tower and museums like the Rodin, Musee D'Orsay and Invalides Militaire (Napoleon's tomb). The neighborhood was very safe as well and there were never any concerns about safety, even late at night.The rooms were very clean and neat. Thank you to the cleaning staff!Amandine also helped us book the Eiffel tower dinner/cruise on the Seine/show at the Lido which was the perfect combination of things to do while in Paris (not to mention a perfect birthday celebration!). That package encompassed 3 of the many things we wanted to do while in Paris.And I can't forget to mention that the hotel also helped by booking the YELLOW van to pick us up at CDG to bring us to the hotel. We received very clear directions on what we needed to do, once we landed in Paris, to ensure we met the driver (needed to pick up any phone and dial the toll free number BEFORE we went to baggage claim.. The man on the other end spoke english, who then told us what door to meet him at). I had been nervous about this procedure, as I couldn't understand how we would be able to make a call, without putting in any coins or using a telephone card, but it worked very easily.Last but not least, Estelle has been helping us contact Thalys, the high speed train to/from Brussels, to see if they found a print of Brugge we inadvertently left behind on the train, when we arrived back in Paris. Thalys hasn't been very responsive to her messages yet, but we are very appreciative of her efforts on our behalf. We are hoping for the best. We gave her our email address as we were checking out the following morning to head back to the States and she said she was going to keep trying to see if she can get some answers for us. This just shows us that the staff at Duquesne Eiffel are truly customer service - oriented.We highly recommend this hotel because of its location, and staff and cannot wait to stay again when we are visiting Paris (and hopefully it is sooner than a 20th wedding anniversary!) Thank you, thank you, thank you...

<Author>SolidFred
<Content>Sweet Little Place Nice, comfortable, warm 3 star hotel near Ecole Militiare and Rue Cler. Easy to get to - just a block and a half from a metro stop. But far away enough from the busy streets to be relaxed and quiet. Older building with a small lobby with sofa's and a small bar. Old style spiraling staircase and very small elevator. Front desk staff speaks multiple languages and were fairly knowledgeable.Rooms small, but not claustrophobic. Warm colors, my wife and I were in a room with yellows and blues; our sons with reds and yellows. Closets quite small. Bathrooms nice - modern fixtures and hair blower. Windows kept out the street noise and mattresses comfortable. Breakfast buffet in basement worth the price - 11 euro I think. Coffee, eggs, bread, cheese, yogurt, cereal, etc.Neighborhood close to Eiffel Tower. Rue Cler blocks have fabulous shops - bread, cheese, and pastry shops plus several cafes. Larger corner cafes have the street scene. Nearby small restaurants - wonderful.No hesitation in recommending this hotel.

<Author>Franc0Phil
<Content>Nice hotel, good location Ours was a large party--adults and grown children on holiday, booking 6 rooms. We found the hotel to be exactly as billed on websites. Staff and owner fluent in English, very gracious and accomodating. Rooms are average Parisien (i.e. small) but well appointed, and bathrooms clean and modern. Consider this a safe bet for moderate priced English friendly hotel.

<Author>Paints
<Content>Minor Grievances My dream was to visit Paris. For my honeymoon, my husband and I decided to go to Paris for 5 nights and Greece for two weeks. I decided to start my search for a hotel through Trip advisory. Even though this hotel was only a 3 star hotel, we decided that the reviews were too great to pass it up. I definitely wanted a superior room with a view of the Eiffel Tower. My french is not the greatest so a asked a dear friend who is Parisian to call the hotel and find out how we can be guaranteed a room with a view from the bedroom. She called and we followed their instructions when booking our hotel. The reception assured us if we asked for a certain room in our booking, it would be given to us because we were booking 8 months in advance. Even after the hotel was booked, our friend called the hotel to confirm we received a room with a view. You can imagine our surprise when we did not receive this room. When we went down to the front desk their answer was that we must have misunderstood them when we booked and a room with a view is not guaranteed. I don鈥檛 understand how one Parisian cannot understand another, there is no language barrier. Other than the view, the room was o.k. and the area was great. Most of the staff was helpful, yet if you have a complaint, do not expect much, there is a complete attitude change. I would recommend this hotel if it is just a family visiting Paris, but if it is a romantic getaway I would try somewhere else.

<Author>sohrmurphy
<Content>Loved this hotel! We stayed at the Hotel Duquesne from June 8-16, 2007 and we couldn't have been happier. Julie, Amandine, Allain and the rest of the staff were so friendly and helpful. The superior room we booked (Room 44) was very spacious, clean and comfortable. We enjoyed opening up the wonderful french door-style windows and gazing out at the Eiffel Tower from our room. We also enjoyed sitting at the cafe tables outside the hotel watching the ET sparkle every evening. We changed our money at the hotel for a good rate and no fee. The staff booked tours and airport shuttle for us, answered every question we had and the large bathroom with tub and shower as well as fresh towels and face cloths each day were a luxury that not all European hotels provide. Wifi internet worked smoothly on my laptop and they also have a computer in the lobby for patrons to use. Many cafes, restaurants (Thai nextdoor was excellent!), boulangeries, Shopi grocery store, fruit stands, Invalides gardens (perfect place to eat strawberry tarts and eclairs chocolat for breakfast in the mornings) are all within a couple of blocks from the hotel. We also enjoyed the breakfast downstairs in a lovely setting and even tho some commented that it was expensive, it was far and above your usual continental breakfast since they served buffet style scrambled eggs, ham, bacon, all types of breads, croissants, pastries, jams, yogurt, cereals, coffee, tea, juices, et. We will definitely return and stay at this hotel again! (soon hopefully!)

<Author>Georgia82
<Content>It was all a bunch of lies. Superior does NOT mean a guranteed view! If you're picking this hotel, because you want to see the tower out your window, DON'T! We were so excited about staying at this hotel based on the reviews. We'd seen the candid visitor photos where you can see the eiffel tower from the window of your room. IF you booked a superior room. So, we made sure to book 2 superior rooms, so that my husband and I, as well as grandma and the kids could both have a spectacular view of the tower from our room. We booked months in advance. But apparently, booking early doesn't get you any consideration. Imagine our incredible disappointment when we arrived to find that the room for Grandma and the kids #35 did have a good view of the tower, but the room that they put me and my husband in , #54, did NOT have a view of the tower. When I went downstairs, to ask to be moved to the room that they'd advertised, the clerk slammed things around, and informend me that yes, the room WAS a superior room. I just had to GO OUT ON MY BALCONY, and look way around to the right, and then I could see it. First, if you're at all afraid of heights, there's no way you're going out on that balcony. Second, you can't stay out there, it's far to narrow. The hotel staff was COMLETELY unconcerned that the romantic evening they'd advertised was in fact a lie. In fact, there are only 3 rooms in the hotel with a view of the tower out your window as they advertise, but many more than that with NO view of the tower out your window that they classify as SUPERIOR. So, if you think that you're going to get one of the good ones for certain just because you book a superior room, DON'T COUNT ON IT! You're really paying for a CHANCE that you get a room with a real view of the tower. Also, if you do stay at this hotel, the breakfast room is like an oven. I'd eat somewhere else.

<Author>IsaacBlue
<Content>Charming hotel close to the Eiffel My partner and I stayed at this charming hotel in April 2007 and were completely won over by all aspects of its hospitality. First of all, the location is ideal as it is close to the Ecole Militaire Metro (in the 7th arrondisement) with many wonderful cafes nearby for breakfast, lunch and dinner. Les Invalides (Napoleon's tomb) is practically a stone's throw away. The rooms themselves are quite spacious for a Paris hotel as I've stayed in places in Paris before that were slightly bigger than a kitchen drawer. The rooms look as if they've been recently renovated with marble/granite bathroom countertops that are nicely cleaned everyday. There is a good breakfast - I particulary appreciated the fresh fruit - and all the amenities one could expect in a hotel (i.e. soap, lotion, dryer, internet, etc). Above all, however, I must single out the staff who were all exceptional. Muhammed, Amandine, Estelle and the cleaning and wait staff were a delight to deal with and they went out of their way to be pleasant and helpful. (How Parisians get their reputation for being snotty, I'll never know, but I'm guessing it has as much to do with the visitor as with the way the French respond to certain attitudes). The cherry on the cake, of course, was the view of the Eiffel Tower from our rom with its glorious shimmering lights at night. I think you have to have a corner room to see it; so, ask for rooms 25, 35 or 45. This is a gem of a place and I wholly recommend it to anyone visiting Paris in the near future.

<Author>mattina
<Content>This is a gem! After weeks of looking online for hotels in Paris, I have to say I was rather dishartened. We wanted a good quality, three star hotel in a good location, but most hotels seemed either very expensive (in most cases overpriced, I'm sure) or just poor in quality. Because we were quite late with our booking as well, finding a good one (I was very careful to read reviews on all possible places) seemed pretty much impossible-- that is until my boyfriend stumbled upon Duquesne Eiffel. We both had a good feeling about the place, based on reviews in particular, and we were definitely not disappointed! First of all, the LOCATION IS GREAT. I cannot emphasize this enough. It is close to the Eiffel Tower and a stone's throw away from Napoleon's tomb (hotel des Invalides) right next to the military academy. 5 minutes away is the metro station and along the way a wonderful little bakery and a couple of restaurants. While it is so close to two of the main tourist attractions in Paris, its still a very quiet, nice and safe area. With the metro you can get anywhere in within minutes and even walking to the Louvre is possible! As we arrived we were greeted by a polite young receptionist and she quickly confirmed out booking, filled in the paperwork and gave us our key. The room was on the third floor (there's only 5, its very cosy and nice, clean and charming) and we were absolutely thrilled when we got in, saw the room and especially our view! Now, the room was small, but for a weekend trip this shouldnt be a problem unless you are fussy about space. It was nicely decorated (blue and yellow), everything was good quality and clean and the overall feeling was very charming and French! The bathroom was a very positive surprise because it had a big window and a bathtub, all very modern and tastefully done (nice bathtub and new showerhead). And now to the view- from both windows (room and bathroom) we had a view of the Eiffel Tower! This, I imagine even in Paris, is by no means standard and I'm sure many people pay a lot more than we did to have it! It was so gorgeous at night (although the cynical Parisians apparently disagree ;) and an incredible perk for an already positive experience. We stayed for 3 days and have no complaints at all. We didnt have the breakfast though (which seems expensive-- its much nicer to go to a local bakery, I think), but all and all service was excellent (cleaning and receptionists) and our check-out was very quick and professionally handled. We both loved Paris and a big part of this was thanks to our very positive experience at the Duquesne. I WOULD ABSOLUTELY RECOMMEND THIS HOTEL for anyone looking for a charming, private and conveniently located medium-range hotel- in fact, I'm sure it beats many hotels with more stars and fancier addresses- that's how good I thought it was!  
<Date>Jan 30, 2007

<Author>travelmot
<Content>Great hotel! My husband and I stayed at the Duquesne for 3 days in early October and we had a wonderful time. We opened the door to our corner room on the 1st floor and the room was spotless with a clear view of the Eiffel Tower. We arrived after midnight and the guy at the front desk was very welcoming. His English was ok but he had said that breakfast was included in our price. Apparently it wasn't since at check out, we noticed breakfast was tacked on to our final amount. And at quite a hefty price too. That was the only issue though. Not sure on the size of the other rooms, but the corner rooms are generously sized (ask for a room that ends with a 5 which are the corner rooms). The shower/sink is separate from the toilet, but both were very clean. The Metro is just 2 blocks away (Ecole Militaire stop) and there are a couple cafes along the street. There is quite a bit of street/traffic noise during the day, but the windows actually do a great job in minimizing it. We had a hard time finding the street upon arrival so make sure you have good directions, perhaps from the hotel. Overall, had an excellent stay at the Duquesne.

<Author>Adam R
<Content>Perfectly acceptable, after gaining entry.. I was recently in Paris for a conference and stayed for five nights at this charming hotel not far from the Eiffel Tower and les Invalides. The service was extremely friendly and consistent. Breakfasts were solid and the location was good for some tourist things, although not fantastic for others (most nearby dining was tourist oriented and there wasn't much access to authentic local happenings). The only problem - and it was considerable - was my room key/door. After my first night, my key stopped working. The staff were most accommodating, although it became quite annoying to have to ask someone to be let into my room each and every time I needed to enter it. Also, I had some security concerns as a result of this as no one ever asked for ID before opening my door. Of course, this could be because they had excellent memories, but I'm skeptical. So, after one decent night, I had four questionable others. I'd recommend this to someone who wants to stay near the tower, but don't stay in room 11.

<Author>jdcooper
<Content>Very good hotel with a few minor hiccups The staff at this hotel are lovely. They were extremely friendly and helpful. We had a few hiccups during our stay which they smoothed out with a smile as quickly as possible. (Some issues with the room key, and also our reservation was mistakenly taken down for one night rather than two.) They were also helpful with restaurant reservations, metro directions, etc.We stayed in two 'superior' rooms at 180 euro per night. The first was pretty basic but acceptable - certainly nothing overtly super about it - clean to a reasonable standard but not to, say, 5 star standard. There were some scuff marks on the walls, slight peeling, etc, but the room did appear to have recieved care, just to be a little bit aging. The second was room 56, with a little balcony and a stunning view of the Eiffel Tower from the desk and from the bed. This room was much preferred! I'd ask for it by number if I stayed here again. The rooms are average European hotel sized, which Americans will find relatively small. This being Paris, you won't spend time in the room anyway.For our purposes, the location left a bit to be desired - however, we are a bit of a party couple in our late 20s and we like to be able to walk to nightlife. On the other hand, it's a 5 minute walk to the Metro and the hotel is in a lovely, quiet neighborhood. It was also quite easy to take a taxi back to the hotel provided one can remember how to say '23 Ave Duquesne' in French at the end of a night out!If I were looking for a peaceful relatively inexpensive hotel in Paris I'd definitely stay here again. I'd send my parents here, for example. But next time we come we will probably try to stay somewhere with a bit more street life. PS -I'd have to say the Rue Cler is our least favorite place in Paris by a wide margin. It's full of tourists from Ohio talking loudly in English and generally being annoying. No wonder people have a hard time in Paris when they act like that!

<Author>Futuredesigner
<Content>Completely exceeded expectations We made a decision in July to go to Paris in September. Hotels recommended by friends were booked, but the Dusquene Eiffel was available. The great Trip Advisor reviews clinched it. The only room type available online was the comfort double, but the attentive staff responded with the offer of an upgrade to a superior room. Based on reviews, I chanced requesting Room 55, and it was available for four of the five nights we wanted. The fifth night was in room 25. The room and the hotel were wonderful. All rooms ending in 5 are corner rooms with views of the Eiffel Tower through french doors. Room 55 at the top of the hotel has the best view and a two-sided balcony from which you also can see Sacre Coeur and Les Invalides. The star attraction, of course, is the Eiffel Tower. At night, it sparkles in your window on the hour with the lights installed for the Millennium celebration. Magical, and surely one of the best views in all of Paris. Room 56 next door is smaller but also has direct views of the Tower from the bed. It would be nice if the hotel would put flower boxes and a couple of small chairs and a little table on the balcony. That would make it perfection.The hotel staff is everything the reviews say and more. They are knowledgeable, friendly, helpful and cheerful and will gladly suggest and make reservations at restaurants and even provide a computer-generated map to them. Even though we had been to Paris before, we really appreciated the advice of the staff. Special kudos to Amanda and Pritti.As others have said, Rue Cler is just a couple of blocks away behind the Ecole Militare Metro stop. This is a great place for coffee and a pain du chocolat in the morning though your table mates may be Americans armed with Rick Steve's Paris guide. There are wonderful cheese and chocolate shops and a nice patisserie. At the Ecole Militare Metro stop there is a small supermarket with a good selection of wine, fruit and staples.Use the Metro and invest in the Paris Visite pass, which is good for one to five days of unlimited public transit rides and discounts to some museums and attractions. Buy them at the Metro stations.We like mussels and went to one of the many Lyon de Bruxelles restaurants. It's a chain, but if moules are your passion, they are good and reasonably priced here. The nicest restaurant experience of the trip was at Fermette Marbeuf (5 Avenue Marbeuf). Its domed ceiling and tile work were enchanting and the food was superb. There's a 30 Euro fixed-price menu that is well worth selecting. We embellished it a bit, added wine and coffee and the tab was only 101 Euro, service included, for a special night of elegant service and wonderful cuisine.All in all, a lovely time at a lovely hotel with a lovely staff and a lovely view. A few reviewers seemed disenchanted with their rooms, but they seemed unused to the size of European hotel rooms and the prevalence of glass half-doors on showers. True, some of the rooms at Dusquene Eiffel are small and more basic, but if you can plan a little request room 55 or any of the corner rooms ending in 5. You won't be disappointed.

<Author>anna9999
<Content>average hotel Loved Paris but not the hotel . My husband and I stayed here for 4 nights. We had the standard double room since ttheir superior rooms were all booked out. So, no view of Eiffel Tower from room. Good location with easy access to the metro Room was small. Less than a 10x10 sq ft. Our bed was 2 twins pushed together which gets uncomfortable at times. However, room's window is soundproof. Blocks out all the street noises. A/C in the room didn't work but that didn't bother us since weather was cool the whole time we were there. Bathroom was small with peeling paint . Bathroom floor floods everytime either one of us take a shower due to it's half shower door. Tub size is standing room for one person. Hard to move around without bumping into the wall. Room does have LCD tv with CNN and BBC channels plus free porn channel after midnite. Overall, this is a good value hotel for the budget conscious travellers since it's located in the 7th district and within walking distance of Eiffel Tower. Wonderful front desk staff. Always courteous, friendly and made us feel welcome.

<Author>Mrhreid
<Content>Duquesne-tastic! We stayed at the Duquesne hotel for three nights in early August. Really liked the hotel - in a superb location near the eiffel tower. Staff were really friendly and helpful - they also spoke excellent english which, while embarrassing as our French is so awful was really helpful. We arrived really early and got checked in straight away which was a bonus. Room was very clean and well equipped with safe, lcd tv and mini bar and a fabulous view of the Eiffel tower (if you hung out the window!!). Only criticism was the room was very small and quite hard for us to move around - the reason i didn't give this 5 stars.The inclusive Breakfast did the job and coffee was top quality - just what you need for packed sightseeing days in Paris. Everything you need is close by - metro, open top bus tower, some good restaurants - would particularly recommend Le Fontaine de Mars. The bar in the hotel was very cheap and you can sit outside with a view of the Eiffel tower and a reasonably priced drink - a rariety in Paris!The area is not the busiest and you feel a wee bit out of the heart of things but after a busy day it's no bad thing Great hotel that was ideal for our holiday!

<Author>ElGrant
<Content>Tres chic! My husband, my son and I spent a long weekend in Paris, staying at the Hotel Duquesne. We had spent a lot of time looking for a good, reasonably priced hotel, close enough to some of the major attractions. We were not disappointed. Our room had a fantastic view of the Eiffel tower, and was walking distance from the Rue Cler, with its marvellous restaurants. The Metro was also just a quick stroll away, and the Ecole Militaire and the Hotel les Invalides within spitting distance. The staff were friendly and helpful (even offering to post postcards to family abroad for us). They also had valuable advice on what to see and where to go. The only part of our stay we didn't enjoy, was leaving. Other than having to say goodbye to gorgeous Paris, we forgot one bag (containing our house keys!) at the hotel, and had some difficulty in retrieving it, as the hotel wasn't happy to package and forward it to us. Other than that, we were pleased with the value for money this hotel represented. We'll be back!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Magnifique I am sitting in the reception of this charming hotel, waiting to go to the airport. What a brilliant time to write this review.Paris:  It has been a very hot five days. I usually visit paris in autumn, so summer was a bit of a shock. It is very hot and very busy. However, this means there is more to do. More street entertainment, longer evening hours to relax with a glass of wine in an outdoor terrace and more people to meet. The area around the hotel is perfect. You can easily visit the eiffel tower, military school or invalides as the encircle the hotel. 5 mins walk takes you to some lovely restaurants with great service ( La terrace is excellent) and food and the metro ecole militaire. I also highly recommend the haircdressers next door to the left. I got a great cut, friendly conversation and a pleasant experience.The area is also very safe at night and the hotel has 24hr reception.Hotel: On our first night we were greeted by a friendly receptionist who gave us all the information we could need and also gave us a safety warning about venturing onto the champs elysees whilst france played the quarter finals. The hotel has 5 floors, and 58 rooms. The lift to the floors is very very small, just enough for 2 people and small bags. We stayed in room 58, which was very small and had a view of the back of buildings. However, this hotel is listed at 150 euros a night, and we paid much less then this through midashotels[--]. Therefore, we had a lovely hotel in a great location with a ok room. The TV was LCD, the bathroom marble, the room cleaned every day with fresh towels and the option of breakfast in bed.The breakfast is 11 euros each, and there is some nice patisseries or supermarches nearby to get a croissant cheaper. However, our fantastic price also included brekkie. You simply went doen each morning or rang for a continental tray to be brought to the room, with no extra charge. It has a croissant, pain au raison, pain au chocolat, bread, butter, jams, honey, and orange juice. Bliss! The bathroom, despite being marble would be very difficult for anyone with poor mobility or a larger disposition as the space to get into the shower is tight, high and narrow. The room is air conditioned to perfection, an absolute MUST in Paris in summer.In summary, I highly reccommend paris as a destination, but especially stay in this hotel. Its cool, quiet and safe. I have stayed in much noisier areas and not liked it. The 7th arrondisement is perfect.

<Author>LincolnNavigator
<Content>Great unpretentious hotel We just returned from a ten day trip to Paris to celebrate my daughter's graduation from high school. There were five of us: two parents, one 14-year-old boy, and two jubilant 18 year -olds. We rented an apartment in the 7th arrond. but could not stay the last two nights as it was already rented, so we booked the Duquense Eiffel as it was close by. The first thing I noticed about the hotel was how friendly and helpful the staff was---everyone at the desk spoke English and were very patient with our questions. When we first arrived, the desk person asked if we would like to see several of the rooms in order to make our own choice. Then, she made sure that she could book two rooms side by side so we could keep track of the 18 year-olds (!). The rooms are not posh, by any means, but they are decorated nicely and the bathrooms are above average for a small hotel. We stayed in a triple (with our son) and the girls had the other twin room. The triple was a tight fit, especially with open luggage, but it all worked our well. The TV was fine, and we watched the World Cup tournament on a couple of nights. Two best features about the hotel: 1) when the windows are closed, you cannot hear a sound outside! This is a miracle in noisy Paris and was much better than the apartment we rented. We all slept deeply and well. 2) when we left the room for the day, we left our clothes strewn about, but when we returned everything had been folded nicely into our bags, the beds were made, and the room tidied. It was great! Finally, we did not have a direct view of the Eiffel Tower, but if we stood and looked sideways out the window, there was the symbol of Paris, all lit up like an upside down bubbly champagne flute. Magical!I would recommend this hotel to anyone who is not seeking something fancy or luxurious, just a great, nice, quiet, solid hotel with a superb staff.  
<Date>Jun 20, 2006
