<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>It's pronounced "Du-Cain" All the previous reviews were right on! This place was great. Quiet, comfortable, very clean, and the staff, specifically, Pretty, were extremely helpful. We booked a superior room in advance, and were not disappointed, on the first floor, room #15, with a great view of the Eiffel Tower. If you are late for breakfast, you will not get any ham ;-) The windows to the street had great sound supression which really kept out the street noise...Great water pressure in the shower, with consistent temperature.Now onto 4 great tips, and under-the-radar secrets, which made our trip quite memorable: 1) La Terrace, a local restaurant, 2 blocks north of the hotel, on the corner of Duquesne and Ecole Militare...which is where the nearest metro stop is. This brasserie provided great meals for either lunch or dinner. 2) Le Zimmer, our favorite restaruant, with the most amazing Chateaux Briand ever! We went two nights in a row. On the right bank just across from the Latin Quarter, it is conveniently located on the north east corner of La Place de Chatalet, again right across from the metro. They even had a non-smoking section. 3) An evening concert at Saint Chapelle. Look for the flyers or posters outside of the entrance gate. Purchase your tickets early in the day for the evening concert. Our experience was a 6 piece orchestra ensemble, with a wonderful opera singer, performing Vivaldi, only amplified by the accousitcs of a 400 year old church. Nearly everyone was brought to tears. It was one of our highlights for sure! 4) All inclusive metro/all-access day pass to Versailles. These tickets must be purchased at the RER station (appox. 21 Euro), and will give you priority entrance, avoiding the huge crowds waiting to get in. We also highly recommend the guided tour, which tours areas which can't be seen on the audio tour. After very long days, it was always a pleasure coming back to the Du-Cain!  
<Date>Apr 28, 2006

<Content>Perfect Hotel for an Affordable Price..... We stayed at the Duquesne Eiffel hotel for one week and loved it. The staff was very friendly and helpful. My only criticism was the room service. They didn't adequately replenish towels, cups and some of the basics. But other than that it was a great little quaint location. NO PETS ALLOWED IN THIS HOTEL...Good affordable local restaurants...In walking distances of Invalides, the Effiel, Musee de la Marine, Palais de Chaillot, local shops and the metro. If you're American do not expect big rooms, their rooms are very small even by economy hotels standard in the States. Enjoy Paris wherever you decide to stay.

<Author>Jenn65
<Content>Just OK My family stayed at the Duquesne for 4 nights - we used 3 rooms on the 4th floor. I am really torn as to my review of this small hotel. On the one hand, the place was extremely clean and in a great location. Close to the Eiffel Tour and des Invalides - many small cafes and markets. We enjoyed walking around the hotel neighborhood very much. The desk staff spoke English well and was helpful with directions, taxis and advise. BUT - I found the rooms very small with horrible, shabby sheets and towels. Twice we had to request towels and even toilet paper! The maids rarely replenished items like plastic cups, wash clothes and the honor bar. Also - the hotel is poor on service. We gave them a small amount of laundry that was promised back to us by 8pm. At 10pm we called the front desk to inquire and were told that we would have to come down and get it ourselves. I know this is a small 3 star hotel - and perhaps we expected too much - but I will try to step up to a better service hotel in the future.

<Author>jdf3361
<Content>Nice hotel in Paris for the right price I spent 3 nights, with two rooms, at the Duequesne Eiffel. The location of the hotel is excellent - close to metro, Invilades, Eiffel Tower. There are many local bistros, sidewalk cafes within a 2-3 block radius. The area was safe and walking the neighborhood at midnight did not seem uncomfortable at all. Pricing was in the $200/night range which I found very reasonable in Paris. The smaller of the two rooms is SMALL. The larger of the two rooms was adequate and typical for a large city hotel. The hotel was spotlessly clean, in excellent state of repair. The front desk spoke English, was always helpful and added to the pleasure of staying here. If you don't want to drop a fortune on lodging in Paris, this is genuinely a nice hotel to park for a few days.  
<Date>Jun 12, 2005

<Author>lindagettins
<Content>loved the french people been back home four days. we had a fab time in paris, it was our first time. hotel DUQUESNE EIFFEL was brilliant. we booked a superior room could not have been better positioned. room 35, it had two windows, one to the main road the other faced the eiffel tower. WOH,what a site on a night time all lit up and sparkling. the rooms where very comfortable with a king size bed, tv,mini bar (which at first thought was expensive but then realised all paris was) all of the drinks in the mini bar was well known brands. the bathroom  toilets were very clean, lovely white towels every day. the only thing i would pick on (and this is really being picky) there was no tea  coffee facilites in the room this would have made it perfect. in there defense i did e-mail them and ask this and was informed i could ask for hot water at any time.there is one other thing, when we arrived i asked which one of the 2 rooms i booked was the non smoking room, the receptionist said smoke in either room. if i had gotten a room which people had been smoking in this would have ruined my holiday i think the management of the duquesne eiffel need to put this problem right or there is no point in advertising non smoking rooms. this apart we had a fab time and would definently go back to this hotel.

Only two blocks to metro and five minutes walk to Eiffel Tower.
